Supervisory Committee Member Liu Shengyang's Wife Sues for Invalid Divorce Agreement, Yesterday's Special Second Court Hearing, Liu Shengyang Resolutely Unwilling to Mediate 158

Liu Shengyang, also known as Hou Wu, 46 years old, a native of Chaoyang, Guangdong, a current member of the Central Supervisory Committee, residing at 172 Julai Da Road in the French Concession, is now being represented by lawyer Hu Jue by his fellow villager Liu Huang Zhenyuan (age 40), residing at 19 Qingfu Lane, Pushi Road, French Concession, who has filed a lawsuit in the civil court of the Special Second Court, claiming that although it is different to not accept advance payments for fraud, please mediate. It is claimed that the petitioner married the defendant in Guangdong on September 23rd of the Republic of China Year 7, and was married by Pastor Yang Shoushan. They lived together and had a daughter in Year 16, named Shensheng. Both sides

were very affectionate.

In the 19th year of the Republic of China, the defendant falsely claimed that he was going to Guangdong for official duties and instructed the petitioner to take 1,500 yuan from his friend Zhang Xingyuan for household expenses. When the petitioner went to Mr. Zhang to get the money, Mr. Zhang said that a receipt must be left. If he was illiterate, he could also leave a fingerprint to be handed over to the defendant as proof (the original illegal divorce certificate was presented to the court during the hearing). Unexpectedly, the defendant went away and never returned, maliciously abandoning the petitioner and placing her in a desperate situation. At that time, the petitioner did not know that the defendant was using deceptive means to divorce, leaving the petitioner and her daughter

to depend on each other for life.

Pawning possessions for a living, year after year, like a crane gone without a trace. Now, he knows that the defendant is a prominent official with many concubines, abandoning the petitioner as old and faded. The petitioner is in this situation, hating not to live. For the sake of her young daughter, abandoned by her father, there is no alternative but to entrust someone to mediate with the defendant, but he ignores it. He was forced to hire a lawyer to send a letter of warning, but the defendant refused with a divorce certificate. The defendant also denied misappropriating the petitioner's

Guangdong Public Bond

prize money of 20,000 yuan in September of the 16th year of the Republic of China, as well as more than 16,000 yuan in household expenses paid by the petitioner over the years, refusing to repay them. The illegal divorce certificate colluded by the defendant with Zhang Xingyuan not only stipulates that a mutual divorce should be in writing, according to the Civil Code, but should also have the testimony of two or more people. In this illegal divorce certificate, Zhang Xingyuan is the defendant's witness, and there are no signatures of two or more people to testify, so it is fundamentally invalid according to law and constitutes the crime of fraud under the Criminal Code. The petitioner has no ability to save herself, in order to maintain

family peace,

she applies for mediation according to law, requesting that the defendant be summoned to court in person, to inform the defendant to return the 20,000 yuan Guangdong public bond prize money and 16,000 yuan household expenses that the petitioner misappropriated, and to confirm that the divorce certificate established by the defendant colluding with Zhang Xingyuan is invalid and should be destroyed, restoring the feelings of husband and wife, etc. The court accepted the petition, and yesterday morning, Judge Liao Yuan summoned both parties to the Civil Court 4 for mediation. The petitioner Liu Huang Zhenyuan arrived with her agent, lawyer Hu Jue. Because the petitioner's

facts and reasons

were spoken in Cantonese, fearing that it would be difficult for the court to understand, her agent lawyer re-explained the process. The defendant's lawyer Mai replied on his behalf that the petitioner's words were not true and were completely fraudulent. The two parties met in the 14th year of the Republic of China. If they said they met in the 7th year, it was not true. As for the place where the two parties met, it was in the Hong Kong Club. At that time, the defendant was working in the political world. After the two parties met and lived together, the petitioner did not want to live together because the defendant lost his job. The two parties then signed a separation

cohabitation agreement

with lawyer's testimony and photos. At that time, the defendant paid 1,500 yuan in foreign currency for the petitioner's living expenses and the child's upbringing. It has been seven or eight years. The defendant heard that the petitioner had another partner and had children. Now that she knows that the defendant is developing, she has asked a lawyer to send a letter requesting mediation. The defendant simply

cannot admit

that the two parties have already separated in the past. How can there be any possibility of mediation now? It is important to know that the petitioner had previously taken photos with the defendant and the defendant's wife. The petitioner knew that the defendant already had a wife. How could there be a remarriage? He also presented the photos to the court. The judge asked the defendant's lawyer if mediation was possible to avoid trouble. He replied that the defendant's side absolutely could not mediate. The court then announced that mediation was unsuccessful and adjourned.

The Puji Sanatorium in Beiqiao Hosted the Press Yesterday 159

The Puji Sanatorium, founded by Lu Bohong, a leader of the Catholic Church in China, in Beiqiao Town, Shanghai, specializes in treating mental and neurological diseases. It is large in scale and well-equipped, and can be hailed as the first in East Asia. It was opened by Mayor Wu in July last year. Up to now, it has achieved excellent results, which have been praised by Chinese and foreigners alike. Yesterday, the hospital invited the press to visit, and Vice President Lu Yingen, chief physicians Yuan Junchang and Sun Cuicun, and Mr. Song Zhiyuan and Mr. Lu Wei were invited to host. The following points are described separately:

Hospital Area

The hospital is located in Beiqiao on Hu Min Road. The Hu Min and Song Hu long-distance buses can directly reach the front door. The transportation is convenient. The area is more than one hundred acres in total. The location is quiet. There are 14 wards built, surrounded by large gardens. The light is abundant, and the air is fresh. The hospital has hired many Chinese and foreign experts in mental and neurological diseases to serve as doctors for diagnosis and treatment. Catholic brothers and sisters from France, the the United States and Germany are hired to serve as nurses. The medical skills are excellent, and the care is attentive.

Well-equipped

Each ward is equipped with hot water heaters, sanitary facilities, and electric bells. The wards are divided into first, second, third and fourth classes and can accommodate five or six hundred patients. For diet, there are Chinese and Western kitchens for guests to choose from. The hospital has built its own water plant to supply drinking water. The water quality is clean. The treatment is divided into four types: (1) taking medicine and injections, (2) outdoor sports, (3) electrical treatment, and (4) steam bath, which are administered according to the symptoms of each patient, with remarkable results.

Number of Patients Treated

The address is 150 acres, with 14 wards, a water plant, sanitary equipment, and steel appliances, medical equipment, etc. in each ward, totaling more than 600,000 yuan. Since the hospital opened last year, it has treated 585 men and women. Of the Chinese and foreign patients, 75 men and women have been cured and discharged, 118 men and women have been partially cured, and more than 260 are hospitalized. The founder of the hospital, Lu Bohong, has always been charitable. In addition to charging fees for the first, second, third, and fourth classes as usual, he also charges a small amount for poor patients and provides free treatment. However, there is a fixed quota. It is said that the hospital is still short of more than 200,000 yuan. It is hoped that philanthropists will be generous in their contributions to benefit patients and their families.

Overseas Chinese in the Southern Islands Hope that the Motherland will Improve Exported Alcoholic Beverages 162

The various regions of the South Seas, because of their tropical climate and heavy humidity, have a very large demand for alcoholic beverages. In the past, Chinese alcoholic beverages, such as sorghum wine, Wujiapi wine, and medicinal wine, were imported to Penang and various parts of Malaya every year, with a very large sales volume, especially in rubber plantations and mines. Nowadays, the sales of Chinese alcoholic beverages in the Southern Islands are decreasing day by day. The reason is that the sales of foreign alcohol and locally produced beer have increased greatly, almost replacing the position of Chinese alcoholic beverages. Moreover, Malayan beer enjoys special tax preferences, so its price is low and appealing. As a result, even Japanese beer finds it difficult to compete. During the prosperous period of commerce in the Southern Islands fifteen years ago, Chinese alcoholic beverages were not improved, so they failed to develop adequately. As it stands now, Chinese alcoholic beverages only account for 30% of sales in the Southern Islands, while foreign and locally produced beer account for 70%. The biggest reason is that Jinshan Brandy (i.e., products from Australia) competes with sorghum wine, Wujiapi wine, and Guogong medicinal wine. However, the packaging of Chinese wine cannot compete with that of foreign wine, and Jinshan Brandy also enjoys special tax benefits, while costs and transportation are lower than those of Chinese wine, making it even more difficult for Chinese wine to compete. Therefore, it is extremely difficult to expand the sales of Chinese wine in the Southern Islands without seeking improvement. Overseas Chinese in the Southern Islands usually care a lot about the overseas Chinese cause, so they should pay special attention to the future of the liquor industry. After all, the annual sales volume of liquor is huge. If we can try our best to recover it, it will not only consolidate the commercial position of overseas Chinese, but also increase the economic power of overseas Chinese. Its relationship is indeed not superficial.

Accused of Enticement and Abandonment, Verdict: Lin Tianji Not Guilty, Jing Youmei's Testimony of Seduction Moves Her to Tears 168

Lin Tianji, a Cantonese and Deputy Director of the Auditing Department of the Central Bank, age 49, residing at No. 24, Model Village, Jiangwan Road, in early August of the 22nd year of the Republic [1933], enticed Jing Youmei, a female student from Peiming Girls' Middle School in Huzhou (currently 21 years old), into sexual relations. Subsequently, they rented houses and cohabited at various locations including No. 55, Yongfeng Lane, North Sichuan Road, No. 20, Ruikang Lane, Beijing Road, and No. 83, Shishan Lane, Baoshan Road. On August 2nd of the 23rd year of the Republic [1934], a son was born, named Zhongzheng by Lin. Recently, due to Lin's

abandonment of the woman after seduction, Jing was left uncared for. Consequently, Jing Youmei's father, Jing Kegong, hired a lawyer to sue Lin in the First Special District Court for the crimes of enticement and abandonment under Articles 240, Section 1, and 294, Section 1 of the Criminal Law. The court had summoned him several times, but Lin was unable to appear due to a business trip to Siam, and the trial was suspended. This has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Now that Lin has returned to Shanghai, yesterday afternoon, Judge Xiao Fen opened a criminal court to summon Lin, who appeared with his

defense attorney, Jiang Yiping, to respond to the charges. First, Jing Kegong stated the charges (already reported previously, so omitted). The court immediately inquired about Jing Youmei's age and date of birth. He replied, "My daughter is currently 21 years old, born on September 23rd of the 5th year of the Republic [1916], the year of the Dragon. She is not yet 20 years old." Then, Jing Youmei recounted the process of being seduced by Lin, saying, "My acquaintance with the defendant was through an introduction by my classmate, Shen Xiluo. At the time, he claimed to be unmarried. After I became pregnant, he urged me to

marry him, saying that he could fulfill his promise after I recovered from childbirth. In July of the 23rd year [1934], I returned to my hometown due to my mother's illness, and on August 2nd, I gave birth to a boy at the Huzhou Gospel Hospital, named Zhongzheng by the defendant. Unexpectedly, he has now abandoned me." Jing Youmei burst into tears while testifying, and also felt sick, unable to stand for the testimony. The court allowed her to sit while speaking. When questioned, Lin Tianji stated that his acquaintance with Jing took place in a room at the East Asia Hotel Company. Jing came with a female friend, and they immediately

rented a house to live together. "As for the child born by the plaintiff, I cannot acknowledge it because the plaintiff has many male friends." He presented a letter from Jing Kegong to him as proof, indicating that Jing Kegong was aware of the situation. He also presented two witnesses, He Jinshi and Huang Yushan. The court immediately summoned them. He Jinshi testified about the circumstances of Jing and Lin's acquaintance. Huang Yushan testified that Jing had borrowed 85 yuan from him to make a coat. Later, when he asked her to return the money, she flirted with him. He once saw her with a

young man, walking hand-in-hand. When he asked who it was, she replied that it was her cousin and asked him not to tell Lin Tianji. Observing her behavior, it was similar to that of a prostitute. Jing Youmei claimed that Huang Yushan had previously borrowed 100 yuan from her. There was a conflict when she asked for it back, so he was now falsely accusing her. The plaintiff's lawyer requested that Huang's statement that she was "similar to a prostitute" be

recorded in the minutes, arguing that Jing was a student of Peiming Girls' School, and Huang was making slanderous accusations. A separate lawsuit would be filed. He also presented a letter from the defendant's nephew to Jing, addressing Jing as "Aunt," to prove her identity. The court, seeing the facts clearly, ordered the commencement of the debate. The verdict was announced in court: Lin Tianji was found not guilty.

Tianjin Customs Installs Light Buoy in the Deep Water Channel at the Mouth of the Hai River, Effective from the 10th of This Month 170

Notice from the Commercial Department of the Inspectorate General of Customs: It has been decided to install a light buoy in the deep water channel at the mouth of the Hai River under the jurisdiction of Tianjin Customs to facilitate navigation. The details of the installation and date are listed below. All merchants are hereby notified. Details are as follows: (1) Name of the light buoy: The buoy is named the Deep Water Channel Buoy. (2) Shape of the light buoy: The buoy is an Argand light buoy, painted black with a red flashing light on top, flashing red once every two seconds, with a duration of three-tenths of a second when lit and two and seven-tenths of a second when extinguished. (3) Function of the light buoy: The buoy is used to indicate the corner of the abandoned Xinlanjiang sandbar waterway and the southern side of the deep water channel. (4) Location of the light buoy: The buoy is 80 feet from the corner of the abandoned Xinlanjiang sandbar waterway. From its location, the direction to the Tanggu signal station flagpole is 336 degrees due north, a distance of 10.9 nautical miles. (5) Installation date: Scheduled for around August 10th of this year, with no further notice issued at that time. (6) Relevant sea charts: Hydrographic Chart No. 1025 of the Naval Department of the Republic of China, Canell, surveyor of the Hydrographic Office.

The boatwoman's ignorance is not worth it

Over the past few months, they had saved over 40 or 50 yuan in hard-earned wages. After paying off debts and buying things, they had over 20 yuan left, kept by Zhou. Robbers Commit Three Consecutive Robberies 181

Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Three Bureau, stated that investigations revealed that Wang, along with the convicted Lu A'er, had conspired to commit armed robberies with accomplices between March 25 and May 17 of this year, robbing Gao Yuan's family at No. 6 Pingliang Road, Wu Xu's family at No. 6 Dongxihuade Road, and Wogen Shun's family at No. 29 Dongyouheng Road, involving property worth 526 yuan. He had also committed similar crimes in the French Concession, for which he was sentenced to three years and six months and released in October last year. When questioned, the defendant denied the three robbery cases. He was ordered to be remanded in custody, and the case was postponed for further review.

Sanmin Road Branch Station Changed to Flag Station 182

Previously, for the convenience of train operation, the Sanmin Road branch station on the Songhu Railway was changed to a road ticket station, dividing the section between Jiangwan Station and Gaojingmiao Station into two road ticket sections. Now, the head of the Chewu Section of the Xihu Section believes that, according to past experience, there is no need to use road tickets at the Sanmin Road branch station. The Chewu Department has decided to temporarily stop using road tickets at the Sanmin Road branch station from August 15 and change it to a flag station. When trains pass through the station, there is no need to exchange road tickets, and the section between Jiangwan Station and Gaojingmiao Station will be re-combined into one route section.

Carters' Association Members Criticize the Mutual Aid Society for Depriving Them of Rights for Supporting the Chen Case, Mutual Aid Society Replies that an Explanation Will Be Provided 183

The Industrial News Agency reports that the carters' association members Cang Gongwen, Zhu Fengxiang, He Wushan, Xu Zhulin, and others were deprived of their rights and positions by the association for supporting the Chen Huizhang case. They sent a letter to the association questioning them. The association has replied, promising to explain at the next board meeting. The letters from both sides are recorded below:

Carters' Letter Criticizes Deprivation of Rights

The carters' association members Cang Gongwen and others, over thirty people, wrote to the Mutual Aid Society, stating, "We, Cang Gongwen and others, felt sympathy for the death of carter Chen Huizhang who was beaten to death by a British sailor. To seek future protection, at 3:30 pm on July 27, at the Western District branch of the Mutual Aid Society, Gongwen and others convened a carter representatives' meeting, which resolved (1) to punish the murderer, (2) to force an apology, (3) to provide compensation, and (4) to ensure that similar incidents do not happen again. Cang He and others were appointed as representatives to the Chen case support group to request support, not only for the protection of fellow carters but also for the survival of the entire nation. As carters' association members and representatives, discussing matters concerning the interests of carters and national sovereignty at the Western District branch of the Human Carters' Mutual Aid Society, the Mutual Aid Society should express sympathy and assist in the process to fulfill its responsibilities. However, the fact that Gongwen and others convened the meeting is undeniable, and the meaning is just. Unexpectedly, on July 30, the Xin Shen Daily published a correction letter from the Western District Mutual Aid Society, arbitrarily dismissing the facts. We do not know what their intentions are. Gongwen and others are very surprised. Such behavior is a deprivation of the rights and positions of 40,000 carters and their representatives, which is intolerable. Therefore, we are writing to you to explain your intentions, and we demand a reply within three days to clarify the truth and dispel doubts, so as to avoid misunderstandings. We earnestly hope for this."

Mutual Aid Society Replies that an Explanation Will Be Provided

After receiving the letter from Cang Gongwen and others, the Carters' Mutual Aid Society immediately replied, promising to explain at the next board meeting. The letter stated, "We acknowledge receipt of your letter to the Shanghai Human Carters' Mutual Aid Society dated August 1. It was immediately forwarded to Mr. Maxi, Chairman of the Board of the Mutual Aid Society. The Chairman replied, 'There are bound to be misunderstandings in the letter, and the meeting procedures were not completed, which is regrettable. This letter has the names of two carter members and one candidate member, and it is necessary to submit it to the Board. A reply will be provided after the next Board meeting.' We hereby reply to your letter and hope you will note this."

Woman and Lover Accused of Abusing Young Daughter 185

Mei Baiying, a 26-year-old woman from Changshu, was once married to Wang Yongting, who died seven years ago, leaving behind a daughter named Mei Xueying, now seven years old. Mei, unable to support herself, engaged in prostitution. Last year, she became acquainted with Shao Yueming, a guest from Nanjing, and cohabited with him at No. 62 Hubei Road. Shao was violent and often beat Xueying severely. Around 9 pm the night before last, he beat Xueying with a bamboo ruler, causing bruises on her face, shoulders, and legs. Mei also aided the abuser. Yang Shi, a cohabitant, could not bear it and sent her son, Yang Wenxiang, to report to the Laozao police station. Detective Sun Dafa went and arrested Shao and Mei, and sent the girl to the hospital, which confirmed that she had been injured. Yesterday morning, police lawyer Wang Yaotang filed a lawsuit in the First Special Court Criminal Court One under Article 286, Section 1 of the Criminal Law for abusing a child under the age of sixteen, causing her inability to develop naturally. Mei Xueying testified that she was beaten by her mother and stepfather and that she was not even given enough to eat. When questioned, the two defendants admitted that they sometimes scolded the girl, but they did not beat her and that the bruises on her body were caused by falls. After reviewing the testimony, Judge Feng Shide ordered the two defendants to be remanded in custody and announced that sentencing would be postponed for one week. Mei will be temporarily placed in the Jiliang Shelter.

Robbing Funds and Shooting to Death: Ling Yangsheng Sentenced to Death 187

Chen Jusheng, a 24-year-old man from Pudong who was the manager of the Xiehe Cleaning Company on Pinlang Road and Maqi Road in West Shanghai, was robbed and murdered on the morning of the 10th of last month. Chen, carrying funds, and the company's accountant, Zhu Zhongkang, went to the company to distribute wages. Unexpectedly, just as they arrived at the company gate, they were suddenly confronted by two bandits who, with weapons, robbed Chen of the 800 yuan in cash he was carrying and shot him dead. Subsequently, the Gordon Road police arrested a suspect in the case, Ling Yangsheng (30 years old) from Jiangbei, and brought him to the First Special Court. He confessed to the crime clearly during interrogation. The news of the pending verdict was reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Huang Risheng presided over the eighth criminal court and announced the verdict: Ling Yangsheng is guilty of robbery and intentional homicide, sentenced to death, deprived of public rights for life, and one bullet and one bullet head are confiscated.

Huasheng Road: Counterfeit Currency Ring Cracked, Thousands of Printed Counterfeit Auxiliary Coins Seized 189

Hua, a Chinese detective from the HSBC police station, learned that someone had organized a counterfeit currency ring at No. 66, Sanyi Lane, No. 452, Huasheng Road in East Shanghai, specializing in printing auxiliary coins of 25 cents of the Central Bank, intending to mix them into the market and disrupt finance. He secretly investigated and confirmed the information. Therefore, at 5:10 PM the day before yesterday, he led Chinese detectives Zhang Desheng, Zhao Ziduo, Cao Jiabao, etc. to No. 66, Sanyi Lane, arrested Gu Fugen from Jiangyin, Zhang Tongshen from Hubei, Wang Agen from Changzhou, and other three people, and seized a printing machine and 2,050 Central Bank 25-cent coins that had been printed, and 4,000 that had been printed on one side, and a quantity of printing ink. They brought the people and items to the police station. Under questioning, they learned that these people had colluded with Yan Liangen from Changzhou, the owner of the Jiuda Printing House at No. 141 Caishi Road in the French Concession, to manufacture the counterfeit coins. Yan was responsible for casting all the printing plates, and the profits would be divided equally in the future. Therefore, they worked with detectives from the French Concession police to continue to arrest Yan, searched and found two printing plates, and brought them back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, Police Lawyer Zhang Tianyin sent them to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court, and prosecuted them in accordance with Article 195, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law for counterfeiting currency. He also stated the case, saying that there were still accomplices at large in this case, and requested a postponement for further investigation. Judge Huang then ordered that the case be interrogated separately. According to Gu Fugen, the organization at that location was initiated by Zai Xiangsheng and Zhang A'er, who are at large, and the four of us who were arrested cooperated. We contributed a total of 47 yuan in capital, Zhang Tongshen contributed seven yuan, and Wang Agen contributed 38 yuan. The counterfeit bills had to be handed over to Zai to take away. I was only helping in the organization. Zhang Tongshen, Wang Agen, Yan Liangen, etc. all gave evasive testimonies when questioned. The court ordered that the case be adjourned for seven days for further interrogation, and the four defendants were returned to the police station for detention.

The 11th Olympic Games

World Games Basketball: Our National Basketball Team Actually Lost to Japan, 19 to 35. The Reason Was Missed Free Throws. The Battle Was Tense; Our Team Was Down by Five Points at Halftime. 190

(Central News Agency World Games Special Correspondent Wireless Broadcast Report) The China-Japan basketball game in the World Games was held in Berlin at 6:00 PM on the 7th. Chinese government representatives Dai Chuanxian, Wang Zhengting, Ambassador Cheng Tianfang, and 600-700 Chinese students in Germany all attended to watch. At the same time, dozens of cheerleaders dressed up and entered the arena to cheer. The magnificent sound heard by domestic listeners when the reporter broadcasted was the cheering of our cheerleaders. Because there were a total of 16 competitions yesterday, the game started slightly later than originally scheduled. The game between the two Chinese teams began after the games between Peru and Egypt.

Our Team's Lineup

Each team is only allowed to have seven players on the court. Our formal lineup is: right forward Mu Zuoyun, left forward Wang Hongbin, center Wang Yuzeng, right guard Wang Nanzhen, left guard Li Shaotang, substitutes Shen Yukong and Wang Shixuan. At the time, it was drizzling. The Japanese players were all very short, but the center was half a head taller than ours and wore glasses. Our coach Dong Shouyi was absent due to illness and was replaced by Ma Yuehan and Li Qingan.

We Open the Scoring

We won the right to choose the court. After the start of the game, the Japanese won the jump ball, but it was intercepted by our side. Mu Zuoyun, Wang Hongbin, and Wang Yuzeng made several decisive passes, going straight into enemy territory. Wang Yuzeng raised his hand and shot, but it went past the basket. The Japanese immediately counterattacked, cautiously. In the melee, our side adopted short, quick passes, but the enemy defended strictly. Mu Zuoyun missed two free throws. Li Shaotang and Wang Yuzeng provided support from the rear. Mu Zuoyun darted under the basket and scored a goal, opening the scoring.

Briefly Taking the Lead

Riding on the momentum of victory, Mu Zuoyun again probed the enemy's defense and missed two more free throws. As the opportunity passed, the enemy cavalry invaded. Our five players defended strictly. Soon, Wang Nanzhen fouled, and the opponent made two free throws, making it 2-2. Then Wang Hongbin fouled again, and the enemy scored two more free throws. Wang Hongbin and Wang Nanzhen tried hard to shoot, but were unsuccessful. The competition between the two sides was quite fierce. Li Shaotang fouled, and we were penalized another point. The Japanese led 5-2. Wang Yuzeng changed his style and tried a long shot, but was unsuccessful. Wang Hongbin tried his best to grab the ball and fell several times. Mu Zuoyun was extremely sharp and scored another goal, making it 4-5. Li Shaotang and Wang Nanzhen were eager to score, but several shots were missed. Wang Hongbin scored a goal, and we took the lead 6-5.

Repeatedly Missing Free Throws

After that, the Japanese made all their free throws, taking the lead 9-6 and 11-6. Our passing attacks were frequent, but it was difficult to find an opportunity to shoot. And fate was not on our side. Wang Yuzeng's long shot went into the basket and then came out. Whenever there was a free throw opportunity, it was always missed. The enemy took advantage of the victory and repeatedly attacked under the basket, scoring two consecutive goals. Wang Hongbin occasionally got a good opportunity and flew in. Mu Zuoyun also tossed in a goal, and Wang Yuzeng added the finishing touch, throwing in another goal with one hand, making it 10-15. The first half ended with us down by five points. Statistically, we missed all 15 free throws.

Shaotang Fouled Out

After switching sides, both teams used their original lineups. At that time, the rain gradually increased. We got the first free throw opportunity but missed. And when our side fouled, the enemy scored every time. Mu and Wang, the two forwards, showed their skillful teamwork. Wang Hongbin scored, making it 12-16. At this time, Li Shaotang was fouled out for the fourth time and was replaced by Wang Shixuan. The competition was fierce. The enemy's defense was very good. We launched continuous attacks, but all shots and free throws were missed. The Japanese asked for a timeout and brought in a defender. The intensity of the game remained high. Our Mu Zuoyun left the court and was replaced by Shen Yukong. The situation did not improve. Before long, the captain and center of the opposing team was fouled out for the fourth time. Wang Yuzeng made a free throw, opening the scoring record for our team's free throws.

Disorganized Lineup

Although we tried hard to attack, we were unable to succeed. The lineup gradually became disorganized. After the Japanese gained possession of the ball, they either made short passes that did not go in to delay time, or took advantage of opportunities to sneak in. Their right forward was short and lively, and scored the most points. Our side suffered repeated defeats with scores of 15-22, 15-26, and 15-28. Although Shen Yukong made some progress, it did not help the overall situation. The enemy's movements became more lively, especially their free throws were very accurate. In the end, we lost with a score of 19 to 35. The competition adopted a double round-robin format. We still have one more chance. We hope the team members will work hard. (Broadcast by the Ministry of Communications Radio at 3:00 AM on the 8th)

Central News Agency Special Correspondent Berlin Wireless Report - Our country's football team lost to England 2-0 and was eliminated, which is very regrettable. Looking at the overall situation, our country mostly used short passes when attacking, which slowed down the advance, making it easier for the enemy to deploy their defense. And the running was slightly slower, and the kicked balls lacked strength. This was the main reason for the failure. In the end, there was nothing that could be done because of being one step away. Our team has tried its best.

Overview of the Fifth Day of Competition - One of the Most Glorious Days in Sports History 212

National Haitong News Agency, Berlin, 6th: Today is the fifth day of the World Games and also one of the most glorious days in sports history, because the World Games achieved more today than on any other day. Outstanding records were abundant. Two world records and one equaled world record were set in one day, and a World Games record was established. It can be called one of the most glorious days in sports history without a hint of exaggeration. The crown of Olympic glory was divided among five countries: the United States, Italy, Japan, New Zealand, and Germany. Each country won a gold medal in track and field today. However, among these sports, the most touching and exciting for the audience was the 1,500-meter race.

The best middle-distance runners in the world gathered together, and the competition was the fiercest ever seen at the World Games. New Zealander Lovelock's overtaking

American athlete Cunningham was no fluke. Lovelock's efforts in the last week were truly astonishing to the audience. As a result, he set a world

record. (Berlin, 6th)

Page 18

Accompanying Notes of the World Games Delegation (Letter 6-1) Special Correspondent Feng Youzhen of the Central News Agency 214

On the way to Cairo

From Massawa to Port Said, there are a total of 960 nautical miles. In between, we must pass through the Suez Canal. The Suez Canal starts from Port Said in the north and ends at Suez in the south, with a total length of 87 miles (some say 104 miles). It is a man-made canal connecting the Mediterranean Sea and the Red Sea. In other words, it is a vital passage connecting the shipping routes of Europe and Asia. The postal ship stops for one hour at Suez. Passengers can either stay on the ship and admire the scenery along the canal, one of the seven great projects in the world, or disembark at Suez, take a car to visit Cairo, the capital of Egypt, the birthplace of Western civilization, and then take a car from Cairo to Port Said to catch up with the original ship. You can have both the fish and the bear's paw, as you wish.

The day before arriving at Suez, the ship initiated the formation of groups to visit Cairo. There were two groups in total, one initiated by Thomas Cook & Son, and the other initiated by China Travel Service. The latter's tour fee was 6 pounds for first class and 5 pounds for first class, while the former was half a pound more expensive. As a reporter from the ancient country that is the ancestor of Eastern civilization, I have long admired Egypt, the birthplace of Western civilization. Especially when I read geography as a child, the pyramids and Sphinx in my mind left a deep impression, and I felt it was necessary to go and admire them. So, I signed up to join the China Travel Service group, with a total of 40 people. On the athlete delegation side, only the three ladies of the sports inspection group, Huang Liming, Chen Yongsheng, and Du Yufei, Mr. Mao Yixin of the Shishi Xinbao, and the reporter, a total of five people, participated. The rest were members of the European sightseeing tour group. The Thomas Cook & Son group also had 30 participants, all of whom were Europeans and Indians.

At midnight on the 16th, the postal ship arrived at Suez and docked outside the entrance of the canal. Looking into the distance, many ships were anchored in the canal, with brilliant lights illuminating the clear water. A gust of cool breeze was blowing, exceptionally refreshing. After escaping the hot currents of the Red Sea, everyone was extremely excited to see this scenery. After checking passports, we disembarked from the ship at 1:30 AM on the 17th and boarded a speedboat to land. The travel agency had previously invited a special guide in Egypt to lead the way. At 2:30 AM, we departed from Suez in eight cars, some with six people per car, and some with four people per car, which was quite comfortable.

From Suez to Cairo, there are a total of 150 miles, with a highway connecting them. This highway is entirely built in the desert, and the project is extremely difficult. The first half has not yet been completed, and it is rugged and uneven. The second half has been paved with asphalt, as flat as the roads in big cities. The desert climate at night is somewhat chilly. We traveled under the stars and moon, advancing in a mighty manner. All we saw was yellow sand everywhere, desolate and desolate. Fortunately, there were many travel companions, so there was no loneliness.

The five people in the same car as the reporter were all members of the sightseeing tour group. One person sat next to the driver. The reporter and another person sat in the front row of the car, and the other three sat in the back row. Relatively speaking, the most comfortable was sitting in the back row. When the car had traveled halfway, it stopped for a rest. When continuing forward, the gentleman sitting in the front row silently sat in the back row. As a result, he had a big argument with one of the people originally sitting there. One said that you should obey the rules and stay in your original seat, and the other said that everyone paid the same amount of money and should take turns sitting. The two sides were fierce and seemed about to fight. In the end, the driver mediated and everyone stayed in their original seats. However, the car broke down less than five minutes after starting again. Everyone had no choice but to squeeze into other cars. These two gentlemen who sought comfort also silently endured the same grievance. This humorous scene, although a very small dispute, fully demonstrated the inferior nature of the Chinese people fighting for power and profit, and not stopping until both sides are hurt. This inferior nature can be said to be the root cause of why Chinese politics cannot get on the right track and society is always disordered. If it cannot be eradicated, the country and society will never have a solution. Perhaps readers will not blame me for being too trivial for wasting ink to write this passage.

Enough with the digression, let's get back to the topic. At 5:00 AM on the 17th, we arrived in Cairo, the capital of Egypt, the birthplace of Western culture, one after another. Because the scheduled sightseeing time was only five hours, after gathering in the suburbs, we passed through Cairo and first went to admire the pyramids and the Sphinx.

Cairo and the Pyramids

Cairo, on the surface, does not look like the quaint ancient capital we imagine, but a completely modern metropolis. The entire city is full of tall Western-style buildings five or six stories high. The outer layers of all the buildings are covered with yellow, which is extremely harmonious and symmetrical with the color of the desert. The streets are very wide and flat, but not very clean. There are extremely many flies, flying everywhere, which makes people unbearable. If we want to find a bit of ancient charm on the surface of Cairo, it is probably only the veils of the women. The women's clothes are all black, and the veils are also made of black gauze, hanging down to the chest, exposing only the eyes. This unique custom of the Hui religion has been maintained and has not yet been eliminated. However, a few modern women have also shown their faces and are not ashamed of not wearing veils.

The pyramids are built on sand dunes, about miles away from the city of Cairo. In the light, we went around Cairo and crossed the bridge spanning the Nile River. Before long, we arrived at the bottom of the pyramids. Colored clouds floated in the sky, reflecting on the desert, showing the color of gold. The first impression the pyramids gave us was very beautiful and lovely.

A paved road has been built from the bottom of the sand dunes to the pyramids, and cars can go directly there. However, traveling to the desert should be a taste of camels. So, everyone got out of the car and switched to riding camels. When the camels kneel on the ground, when people ride on them, they first raise their front legs halfway, then raise their hind legs, and finally straighten their front legs. This three-part movement, carried out one after the other, causes the person riding on it to be thrown back and forth, extremely frightened. Several female travel companions screamed in horror.

The so-called pyramids are the tombs of ancient Egyptian emperors. There are a total of 75 in Egypt, and nine in Cairo. Six of them are smaller, and the other three are very great projects, known as one of the seven great projects in the world. The largest one is called Cheops, the second is called Chephren, and the third is called Menkaure, all of which are the names of emperors.

Cheops was built in 2619 BC, and it has been 4,550 years since then. Chephren is about 50 years apart, and Menkaure is another 50 years apart. It is said that ancient Egyptian emperors enslaved their subjects during their lifetimes to build tombs for them. It took decades to complete the project, and he would die and be buried in the tomb. The next generation of emperors took over and started building again. This continued endlessly, and the people of ancient Egypt had to build tombs for their emperors forever, wasting money and labor, just for the tomb after one person's death. The despotism and ruthlessness of ancient Egyptian emperors can be imagined from this.

Cheops is the largest pyramid in all of Egypt. The construction time lasted a total of 30 years. Ten years were spent on quarrying, because Cairo does not produce stones, and they must be quarried from distant mountains and transported. The remaining 20 years were spent on construction. The labor used totaled 4 million people. The tower is 451 feet high, and the base is square, with each side also 451 feet. The stones used each weigh two or three tons, and they are stacked layer by layer, forming a pointed top. The four corners face the four directions of east, south, west, and north. It has been more than 4,500 years since then, and it has not changed at all. Many modern architectural engineers who have seen it are surprised and do not know what methods the ancient architects used to quarry so many neat stones, how they transported them to Cairo, how they moved them up one by one, and even more, how they used them to build this great building on the desert, which can remain unchanged for four or five thousand years. According to our guide, this pyramid used more than 2 million stones, totaling 7 million cubic feet. If these many stones were used to build a two-yard high city wall, it could surround all of France. The scale of the project can be seen from this.

Because everyone was in a hurry, they only looked at it from the outside, and then went to see the Sphinx. The reporter felt that if he arrived in front of this great ancient site without going inside to explore, it would be a lifelong regret. So, on the way back, he got off the camel alone and walked quickly forward. A door as tall as a person was opened on the northeast side of the tower, and two or three locals were guarding there. Walking in, there were winding corridors. Electric lights were installed inside, illuminating it very clearly. This corridor was thirty or forty steps long, and at the end, there were winding stone steps. According to the guards, the emperor's golden coffin was hidden on top of the tower, and it would take ten minutes to walk up. Because time was short, I had to give up in disappointment. Although the reporter regretted not being able to see the golden coffin, everyone felt that the complexity of the structure inside the tower made them feel the difficulty of the project and the ingenuity of the craftsmen even more.

The Sphinx faces the Pyramid of Chephren and is located below the sand dunes. It is said that this monster is 6,000 years old, but archaeologists believe that it was built at the same time as the Pyramid of Chephren, because the appearance of this "monster" is very similar to the stone statue of Chephren hidden in the museum. It is said that the intention of building this monster was to increase the solemnity of the royal tomb, which has the same meaning as the stone elephants and stone horses in front of the tombs of our ancient emperors. The human face symbolizes peace, and the lion's body symbolizes power, representing the character and authority of ancient emperors. This Sphinx is 60 feet high and 210 feet long. It is also made of many tons of rocks stacked and carved. Looking at it from the front, it is completely a human figure. On both sides of the head, there are triangular hairs. The eyes are carved very deeply, and they are shining. Because of the sun and wind for thousands of years, the nose has collapsed, making it look very ugly. Two giant legs extend from the bottom of the body, and the traces are not very clear. Standing next to it, it is completely in the shape of a giant lion. The art of ancient Egypt is worthy of admiration.

On the right side of the Sphinx, there is also an ancient temple, which is said to have been built by King Chephren. Because time was short, there was no time to go inside to see it. After the entire team of travelers took photos on camels as souvenirs, they went down to a nearby hotel for breakfast. After the meal, they drove to visit an ancient royal palace and a museum.

Educational News

All National Secondary Schools and Civic Education Halls Must Install Radios - The Ministry of Education Orders All Education Bureaus to Comply 215

(Nanjing, 7th) The Ministry of Education believes that all national secondary schools must install radios by December of this year, and civic education halls must install them by June of next year. The deadline is not far away. On the 7th, it specially ordered all education bureaus to urge those who have not yet installed them to install them as soon as possible, and to list all schools and halls under their jurisdiction, whether they have been installed or not, and submit them for review within two weeks of receiving the document. Furthermore, all provinces and cities should pay attention to rural areas when installing radios in the future, so as to ensure that the distribution is even throughout the territory. All primary schools and civic schools in rural areas, regardless of size, should also be urged to install them as soon as possible. All education bureaus should be responsible for raising funds for subsidies for purchasing radios. However, the Ministry of Education will still provide subsidies for border provinces and impoverished areas as appropriate. The measures will be notified after the Ministry has comprehensively reviewed and approved the installation situation reported by each province and city this year, and the Ministry will also order each education bureau to formulate its own fundraising and radio purchase measures and submit them promptly.

The City's Literacy Education Situation Over the Past Year: Over 180,000 Illiterate People Eliminated in the Urban Area; This Year's Program Will Continue Once Funding is Confirmed 216

In order to eradicate illiteracy and promote education throughout the city, our municipal government has allocated 200,000 yuan to conduct compulsory literacy education, aiming to eliminate 430,000 illiterate people in the urban area within one year. Since its implementation in January of last year, it has been a year now. Municipal literacy schools have been run for a total of four terms, with over 180,000 students graduating, nearly half the total number of illiterate people. This year, the program is planned to continue once funding from the Ministry of Education is confirmed. The implementation situation over the past year is recorded as follows:

Implementation Process

The Municipal Literacy Education Committee was established in April of last year, and April to June was designated as a preparatory period to carry out preparatory work. On June 3rd, teachers for literacy schools were examined, with 200 being formally selected and 50 as alternates. Training classes were opened for them. A literacy education promotion week was held, and a survey of illiterate people was conducted. A total of 434,452 illiterate people were found in the urban area. The city was divided into 22 districts. The first term established 220 schools, starting on July 1st and ending on August 31st. The second term established 220 schools, starting on September 5th and ending on November 30th. The third term established 222 schools, starting on December 3rd and ending on February 26th of this year. The fourth term established 217 schools, starting on March 7th of this year and ending on May 31st. A total of 879 schools were established in the four terms.

School Establishment in Each District

The number of schools established in each district during the four terms is as follows: Confucius Temple District: 36 schools, Chenghuang Temple District: 49 schools, Zhonghua District: 50 schools, Gaochang District: 76 schools, Qiubao District: 60 schools, Datong District: 69 schools, Qimei District: 40 schools, Yangjing District: 42 schools, Yinxiang District: 40 schools, Yangsi District: 25 schools, Tangqiao District: 24 schools, Gaoqiao District: 10 schools, Wusong District: 30 schools, Jiangwan District: 24 schools, Yinhang District: 38 schools, Pengpu District: 24 schools, Caojing District: 29 schools, Luhang District: 24 schools, Gaohang District: 25 schools, Zhenru District: 25 schools.

Number of Classes Opened

The first term had 220 schools, with 712 adult classes, 302 children's classes, totaling 1014 classes and 54,542 students. The second term had 222 schools, with 1043 adult classes, 66 children's classes, and 5 advanced classes, totaling 1043 classes and 60,139 students. The third term had 217 schools, with 811 adult classes, 186 children's classes, and 107 advanced classes, totaling 1104 classes and 57,240 students. The fourth term had 222 schools, with 886 adult classes, 178 children's classes, and 21 advanced classes, totaling 1085 classes and 62,011 students. In total, there were 3453 adult classes, 732 children's classes, and 133 advanced classes, totaling 4318 classes and 233,932 students.

Number of Passing Students

In the first term, 34,583 students took the exam, with 20,107 passing, 11,300 failing, 3,176 requiring remedial classes, and 14,120 absent. In the second term, 38,259 students took the exam, with 27,085 passing, 6,268 failing, 4,906 requiring remedial classes, and 17,068 absent. In the third term, 44,386 students took the exam, with 32,155 passing, 8,381 failing, 3,850 requiring remedial classes, and 13,094 absent. In the fourth term, 51,671 students took the exam, with 35,968 passing, 4,865 requiring remedial classes, and 12,133 absent. In total, 168,899 students took the exam, with 115,315 passing, accounting for 68%, 36,787 failing, accounting for 22%, 16,797 requiring remedial classes, accounting for 10%, and 56,415 absent, accounting for 25%.

Situation of Private Schools

The Literacy Education Service Corps trained and passed 4,442 students. The Municipal Party Headquarters supervised literacy schools and passed 22,519 students. Labor literacy schools passed 1,665 students. The Chinese Education Office oversaw literacy schools and passed 2,076 students. In total, 45,695 students passed. The total number of students who passed in private literacy schools in the city was 161,010, with 23,195 requiring remedial classes, totaling 184,205.

Measures for Admission and Transfer of Northeastern Elementary School Students 217

The Northeast Youth Education Relief Office of the Ministry of Education, previously, because students who graduated or studied at elementary schools in the Northeast and entered the customs to study were often rejected by various schools due to non-compliance with the certificates they held, which affected their studies. This was not insignificant. Therefore, interim measures for the admission and transfer of northeastern elementary school students were drafted and submitted to the Ministry of Education to order the education bureaus of various provinces and cities to instruct their subordinates to comply. The method is that those holding elementary school graduation certificates from various provinces and cities in the Northeast after September 18th to apply for junior high school, or the aforementioned study certificates to request insertion into the corresponding grade of elementary school, should be allowed to apply with the certificates they hold. If admitted, the school admitting the student should fill out the northeastern elementary school student academic form according to the format prescribed by the office, and send it to the office together with the original application certificate. The office will then issue a certificate based on the reported academic qualifications and reference to the original certificate, so that the school can report it according to regulations.

The World Chinese Students' Federation held its second talk with students studying abroad yesterday morning at 9:30. More than 50 students studying abroad attended. The secretary-general of the federation presided over the meeting, delivered an opening speech, and reported on the necessary circumstances of organizing groups on the journey, etc. Next, the students studying abroad introduced each other. Finally, Wang Xiangyue, Xu Zongyi, and Shen Yao were publicly elected as representatives to respond at the farewell party for students studying abroad on the 16th. Around 12 o'clock, the group photo was taken and the meeting adjourned.

Era Medicine Journal

Questions and Answers Regarding Various Aspects of Nocturnal Emission and Treatment Methods 221

(Asked by Mr. Yao Yunping, Answered by Dr. Zhou Xiaohan.)

Dear Editor:

My nocturnal emission problem is getting worse and worse. Sometimes I have emissions every day – continuously for more than ten days; and I'm still asleep when it happens, and I'm already finished when I wake up; I've always had emissions without dreaming. During the day, I feel dizzy and almost completely unable to work on brain-intensive and eye-intensive tasks such as reading and writing. Also, I often feel chills and catch colds very easily. Grains: Futures Flour Also Falls Back Sharply 235

Yesterday's flour market saw constant fluctuations in each month's value after the opening of the morning market. The situation was chaotic. Because the price of foreign wheat was good by eight fen in the near term in Chicago but fell by two or four jiao in the far term, and Canadian grain fell by eight fen to two jiao, prices for this month and September fell about one fen during the opening as actual sales were sluggish. However, the price of October and the October month was raised by two or three fen from the previous day's closing price due to short seller panic buying and some business from Southeast Asia as the price had not risen enough the previous day. At the first month's pricing, as factories released product, hearts softened, and by the second pricing session, prices plummeted as customer brokers and outside investors quit, and Tianjin brokers released product, with the trend strong. All fell by two or three fen at the end of the session for the months of October through December, with January falling sharply with no recovery due to the gap in pricing, falling by a massive seven fen from the previous day's high opening price. Looking at the present, at the time for new wheat, the high prices are already a remarkable situation, and if the international grain market changes, the bulls will be in danger.

Sugar Market: Chaoshan Sugar Prices Continue to Rise 246

Yesterday at the Public Association, prices for various types of sugar such as No. 4 coarse sand white and Nos. 4, 8, and 9 East White remained as before, with few buyers. There were no changes in the prices of local factory cotton white brands such as Zhenji, Jinxin, and Renhua. The domestic sugar market remained strong. Guangdong and Chaozhou merchants offered several hundred packages of cotton red sugar, with higher prices at $15.30 and ordinary prices at $14.40. There were over one hundred packages of Huizhou white sugar, priced between $19.20 and $18.60, and one hundred packages of Hainan foreign sugar, priced at $15.45. According to reports from Shantou, production costs continue to rise. Currently, the cost for Shanghai City, including extraction fees, is $14.78 for top-grade blue, $14.40 for top-grade Huanggang blue, and $12.70 for top-grade Longqing blue. Genuine cotton red sugar is priced at $16.60, with an exchange rate of $1,100. According to reports from Zhangzhou, Chaozhou and Shantou merchants are purchasing Diaoqing in Zhangzhou, so production costs have also increased by five or six jiao.

The jointly formed company held its third weekly tender for Guangdong sugar yesterday, with a total quota of over 6,000 packages. Garlic prices remained unchanged. Two hundred packages of Shun De Factory’s Five Rams coarse white sugar were sold at $21.60, another 1,320 packages from Dongguan Factory were sold at $21.50, and another 150 packages from Qu Xi Factory were sold at $21.10. The remaining packages were not sold.

Textiles: Cotton Cloth Shortages Maintain Current Status 247

Yesterday's cotton cloth market situation was such that although the yarn market had seen continuous and significant declines, the cloth market was able to maintain its price level due to a shortage of available goods. The decline was slow. Yarn prices fell by $17 or $18 per piece, while cloth prices fell by only $5 or $6 per piece. Therefore, manufacturers' attitudes have softened, and they are opening goods in line with the market. However, trading houses and dye factories are seeing sluggish sales and weakening interest due to buyer hesitancy. Dongpi white goods, fine cloth, coarse cloth, and fine twill all saw price decreases of 5 fen per piece. Color goods saw fewer changes. Only Sijunzi Zhigong and Biji continued to decrease by 1.5 li per yard. This factory's current autumn goods, including patterned and plain Zhigong, Biji, and flannel, remain very strong. Products are scarce, and buyers are eager to purchase more. Only Dafeng Factory’s Caishen crepe fell by 5 li per yard. Yesterday, buyers from Hunan, Tanzhou, Changsha, and Changde purchased a large amount of Dong goods such as Sijunzi straight satin, totaling over one hundred and dozens of pieces. Previously, Dongpi straight satin Biji from this region used the Star brand mark, but this procedure is no longer necessary. Buyers from Sichuan and Hunan have placed large orders for futures of this factory's Dafeng Guangzhong Biji Zhigong ne flannel, etc. The flannel white flannel from this group was the earliest to be loaded. Business in Zhejiang is most active in Wenzhou and Taizhou. Yesterday, they purchased over one hundred pieces of fine cloth, fine twill, coarse cloth, Biji Zhigong, crepe, etc.

If overseas silk prices can stabilize, then export silk can regain its prosperity.

Seafood: New Dried Scallops' Slow Sales Lead to Gradual Market Easing; Abundant Harvest of New Ningbo Light Mussels 250

The arrival of new dried scallops is gradually increasing, but the volume of sales to buyers has decreased instead. As a result, selling prices from trading houses have gradually eased. Yesterday, the market quoted prices of $68.50 for Dongzhong strips and $70 for fine strips. Tou Chao Shen Jue goods were only quoted at $54. Because market operators still have previous goods in stock, they are temporarily uninterested in further purchases, so there are few buyers. The market is likely to see further price declines.

Most of the new Dong light mussels that have arrived in recent days are of lower grades. The market operators are gradually lowering their prices. Yesterday, goods priced at $62.80 were not only small but also had shrunken bodies and dull colors. Market prices for high-quality goods remained at $78. Fewer were being sold at the current price, but the current market price is $60, and most are willing to sell. This year's domestic Ningbo light mussels have had a very abundant harvest with excellent quality, but not surprisingly, many goods have been shipped, making it difficult to raise prices. The current market price for new seed mussels is $34 or $35, $37 or $38 for sifted clean mussels, and $46 for yuan mussels.

Shen Bao Women's Special

Which Path to Take? 251

— Chen Danxing

At the end of the last semester, many female students have completed their basic education. Stepping out of the middle school gate on one side, and preparing to enter university for further studies on the other, they inevitably face the dilemma of a fork in the road. The biggest problem is how to choose a specialized discipline. Before them lie education, music, art, medicine, sericulture, literature, plus law, physics and chemistry, physical education, transportation, civil engineering, and even military and aviation. In the current extraordinary period, women also have the possibility of research and learning. However, the array of disciplines has dazzled the female students, making their minds waver. Which subject should they choose? Which subject is suitable for them to study? Which path leads to their destination? They must carefully consider this.

The period of solving this problem contains a crucial key to the future life of female students. Many students who love music, however, go on to study civil engineering. Many students who love literature, on the contrary, blindly follow to study physics and chemistry. As a result, they constantly feel a kind of pain that violates their personality. Even if they bury themselves in their studies with heart, there is a discordant trend, achieving half the result with twice the effort. Some change course halfway, the loss of spirit, time, and economy is self-evident. In addition to the recognition of one's aspirations and goals, one must also consider whether one can suit one's personality. If one already has a fiancé, then for the sake of future cooperation in seeking a living in society, one should choose a discipline that is the same as or related to the other party as much as possible, so as not to have conflicting interests in the future, which will not only fail to obtain mutual assistance between husband and wife, but will also lead to adverse phenomena. However, this point cannot be stubbornly adhered to.

Adapting to the needs of the environment is also a criterion for female students to choose a subject. Female students in rural areas, in order to save the decline of the rural economy, must resolve to study sericulture and agriculture. Even if the interest is slightly inferior, they can only sacrifice their own interests and save the public. This is one example. What about other such things as military affairs, aviation? Medical and first aid services are especially needed in China during this extraordinary period. Strictly speaking, studying is not only for oneself, for the family, but also for the society, the nation, and the country. Even music and art are no exception.

Female students who have completed their basic education, various specialties are in front of you, which path do you take? This question must be decided by yourselves, to suit your personality and to suit the environment. Blindly following and experimenting are not right!

Women's Professions and Professional Women 252

— Wang Duan

In China, which has not completely shaken off old ideas, women only have the role of staying at home. On the one hand, parents for their daughters, and parents-in-law for their daughters-in-law, hold the 18th-century notion of "relying on parents at home and relying on husbands after marriage," and do not allow women to run to society to make a living. They think that it is such an "indecent" act for a woman to go outside to do something instead of enjoying herself at home. On the other hand, many women also only know how to enjoy themselves and rely solely on others after finishing their studies at school, and thus abandon their promising lives to live the life of a caged bird. Although there are also those who are not tempted by vanity, but with a firm and indomitable spirit of fearlessness, struggle with the environment and finally achieve victory, and go on the path of a profession.

In China, where women's professions are not widespread, where is the way out for women? A few shops and institutions occasionally employ a few female staff. On the surface, they chant "promoting women's professions," but in reality, they all have bad intentions. Some employ female staff to attract customers, others hire them to relieve the boredom of office life to be used as entertainment, and even borrow the guise of "profession" to carry out their purposes of bullying and toying. They think that women are only things for people to play with and admire, so the derogatory nickname "flower vase" is quickly added to the heads of professional women.

Are all women useless? Are they only worthy of being toys for men? Of course, we absolutely cannot admit this. But where does this come from, and we have to examine it: Look at so many women who come to society to work only with the "showing off" principle, and this is the main reason. Some are even tempted by vanity and spare no effort to abandon their actual lives and pursue them, and eventually fall into a vicious trap and fall; others are self-proclaimed romantic, dressing up in grotesque shapes to flatter the manager, treating the office as a social place; and still others do nothing all day long, only mingling with male staff, flirting and scolding, doing everything. These are, of course, only a minority of the minority, but when women's professions are just beginning, this is at least very unfavorable to other women. These shameless scoundrels eventually implicate others in being looked down upon and despised; women's professions are invisibly further devalued and increasingly declining.

It is a despicable thing to use the promotion of women's professions as a tool to carry out the purpose of toying with women. People who chant "women should go to society" should use an honest attitude to open up a way out for women. At the same time, professional women who serve society, can you endure this insulting title? Do you willingly fail to make progress? No, never, quickly strengthen your will, avoid the temptation of vanity, respect your personality, devote yourself to practical work, contribute to society, and create happiness for yourself. The great road of women's professions with unlimited prospects is waiting for you to develop and move forward!

I Returned to My Family 253

— Xiaoliang

When I graduated from ×× Middle School, I had great ambitions. For the women of our country who have been bound by traditional ideas for thousands of years, I really wanted to do some work of liberation, so that everyone could run out of their families and serve society, to fight for equal and free status for our women.

Fortunately, in the autumn of that year, I found a small position in a bank. The day I went to take office, I was so happy that I thought I could get rid of the bondage from then on and do a little for the women's world.

But it is also pitiful to say, after I had worked for a few months, besides my colleague Ms. Zhang being able to express sympathy for my opinions, the other female colleagues all thought that my ideas were strange. No matter what methods I used to contact them, there was no way. They were all poisoned by modern times. They only wanted to watch movies, talk about love, and pay attention to clothing. When I talked to them about the liberation of women themselves, they would also express headaches and disgust. Even reading books, they only liked love novels. In this way, my ambition in school was weakened a lot. It turns out that Chinese women are so unpromising!

After doing this for more than a year, I fell into the river of love and finally got married in the winter of that year. My husband worked in the telegraph bureau, his salary was sixty yuan, plus my thirty yuan, and our monthly life was very good. But in the second year, I gave birth to a child and couldn't work, so the total income was only sixty yuan. It was impossible to allocate to maintain the two of us, a child, and a nanny. So after a few months, I had to go back to work. But it cost too much money to use a wet nurse for the child, so I decided to let him eat milk powder during the day and I would feed him at night, but this was wishful thinking. The child did not eat milk during the day, and my own milk was so painful. In order to work, I had to let the child eat milk powder completely. Naturally, our expenses increased, and when the two of us were out working, the clothes were washed by the laundry, and we ate mostly outside. Only on Sundays did I cook myself, but now I had to prepare meals every day. The nanny was in charge of the housework, but not only did she not know how to save money, but the money spent each month often exceeded my budget, and the things she did could not satisfy me. Therefore, I had to give up my job and return home.

Now I have dismissed the nanny, and I am doing all the household chores, such as washing clothes, cooking, taking care of the children, etc.

Based on the above facts, I feel that Chinese women must obtain true liberation: first, the modern poison of the current era should be eradicated; second, we should also unite with men who sympathize with us, and jointly thoroughly transform the social system, so that women have the same status as men in society and are not burdened by housework, so that we can truly talk about liberation!
