This Newspaper's Special Feature

A Visit to Dr. Qian Jianqiu 255

— Ji Ping

Among the freelance professionals in Shanghai, lawyers are the most numerous, with a total of more than 1,200 people. Our journalists are less than half their number; there are also fewer doctors than them; and accountants are even further behind. Naturally, there are more men in the legal profession than women. These female lawyers each have their own position and their own strengths. Today, I want to introduce one of the outstanding female lawyers – Dr. Qian Jianqiu. This is not just flattering her. In fact, her thinking, knowledge, and personality can all be models for women. People like this will naturally be respected by everyone. Dr. Qian is currently a member of the Lawyers Association and a professor at Shanghai Law College. She is not only proficient in law, but also has a good foundation in literature and calligraphy. She has also occupied a glorious page in the history of drama. Readers, do you remember the sensational play "The Lady's Fan" twelve years ago? That play broke the box office drought in Shanghai. She played the role of Ms. Jin in the play and said more than a thousand words of dialogue in one breath, which made the audience shed countless tears. Her genius was revealed in this play, and even shocked the whole society. This is truly a miracle.

Director Hong Shen then persuaded her to study drama, but her ambition was not small, and she believed that drama was not the greatest wish after all. In 1929, she went to the United States and entered Northwestern University in Chicago, specializing in law and earning a doctorate. After returning to China, she practiced law. Three years ago, she married Mr. Huang Bi. This Dr. Huang was a good companion who went to the United States at the same time, at the same level, with the same degree, and returned to China with the same path. You can imagine how perfect this marriage is! However, after their marriage, he was an official in the capital, and she worked at sea, separated by a long distance, each fulfilling their duties. Although it is said that children are sentimental, they also treat it calmly. This is another miracle.

Right Picture: Dr. Qian Standing 256

The day before yesterday, I visited her and talked for an hour. The first question was: "What are your views on the new family?"

She said, "The responsibilities of new Chinese women are much heavier than those of men. Men simply work externally, while women not only need to develop their personal new careers but also bear the responsibility of the new family. Isn't taking care of both inside and outside heavier than for men? That being said, the current women have not yet reached the 'new' stage. Everyone knows that in the past, in large family systems, labor and leisure were uneven, and happiness and suffering differed. It fostered dependence and led to a desire to shirk responsibility, resulting in numerous malpractices, which were obviously not as good as the perfect small family system. However, the new family is not without its drawbacks. The most easily discovered shortcoming is the equal attitude of the couple. I believe that a couple must establish an attitude of 'respect and love' and 'understanding.' Westerners value this very much, while we Chinese seem to be somewhat indifferent. If a couple can 'respect and love' each other, they will support and help each other, as if they were two as one. If they can 'understand' each other, any misunderstandings can be turned from major to minor, and from minor to nothing. However, when major matters arise at home, both parties must reach a consensus. One cannot act unilaterally. One should explore calmly and rationally, and one cannot easily abandon one's straightforward views for the sake of 'understanding.' At this moment, one should emphasize facts and reduce emotionality, so as to avoid conflicts and disputes. Regardless of poverty or wealth, the new family should universally adopt diligence, thrift, hard work, and endurance as common principles. It is best not to rely on others for household affairs. If servants are needed in reality, they should be treated kindly and not despised, and they should be trained to be literate and know etiquette. They come from the countryside and have missed the opportunity to study when they were young. If they are not trained, they often have deceitful, irresponsible, and rude behaviors, which are infinitely harmful to others and themselves. There should not be too many children. With too many children, it is difficult to provide comprehensive education. It increases the responsibility of parents and the suffering of the family. Family education must be highly valued. Great personalities are cultivated in small families. People who work hard all day long cannot do without entertainment, but improper entertainment should not exist in the new family. The entertainment I advocate includes: (1) outings in the suburbs; (2) physical activities; (3) attending concerts and gatherings; (4) connection between families with like-minded people; (5) watching noble dramas or movies. As for the responsibilities of the housewife, managing household affairs is the minimum. Further, she should assist her husband's career. Those with superior abilities should give full play to their personal aspirations and do more to benefit the public, ensuring that they take care of both inside and outside without bias, and only then can they be called women of the new era.

When women serve externally, they should not think that since they are women, they should enjoy special rights and do less work or only do light work. This kind of mentality is an inferior mentality that degrades women's status. We rely entirely on actual strength to do things. If we have sufficient ability and real talent, we will naturally be respected, and there is no distinction between men and women.

"What kind of standards should modern young women have for self-cultivation?"

When I raised this question, she pondered for a moment and then gave the following answer: "The circumstances of each person are different, and the standards of self-cultivation will always be somewhat different. I think every young woman should pay special attention to: (1) Virtue has nothing to do with 'new' or 'old.' The sage said, 'Words should be faithful and trustworthy, and actions should be honest and respectful.' This is the foundation of self-conduct and dealing with the world. (2) Develop an independent spirit and eliminate the psychology of dependence. (3) Forge a strong physique. (4) Establish the concept of society and the country. (5) Have a broad vision and not be constrained by trivial matters. (6) Respect one's own personality. One more point: women who have the opportunity to study should never easily give up this once-in-a-lifetime opportunity. Those from poor families cannot afford to go to school, while those who are more well-off should aspire to make progress and not bury their youthful ambitions. They should embrace the aspiration that 'what I learn today will surely be used for society in the future.'"

"From a legal point of view, in recent decades, women in various countries have demanded equal legal treatment and have long achieved their goals. The current laws of most countries have generally adopted the principle of gender equality, and most of the parts that deprived women have been abolished. However, in law, rights and obligations are equal conditions. If you enjoy rights, you must fulfill your obligations. Since the law grants women the right to enjoy equal rights, whether they can actually fulfill the same obligations as men is entirely a matter of fact. The law only advocates it."

"Because of legal equality, I thought of an interesting thing. For example, in terms of women's titles, women's names are often prefixed with their husband's surname after marriage. I wonder if there is any legal basis for this?"

She said, "According to current law, there is indeed a provision that 'a wife prefixes her original surname with her husband's surname,' but this is not mandatory, and the parties can freely use it. In fact, it is very common for a wife's surname to be prefixed with her husband's surname. Some women even do not use their own names after marriage and are only called Mrs. XXX. This kind of title is also very popular in European and American countries. European and American female students often do not use their original names after marriage and are called Mrs. - in social occasions. In my opinion, it is not necessary to prefix the original surname with the husband's surname. Even if the original name is used, there is absolutely no inconvenience."

She finally stated, "The most important issue in China today lies in education. I often feel great sympathy for the aspiring young people who are poor and out of school and the majority of ignorant people. I have a plan in my heart, but unfortunately, I cannot implement it now. Once I have sufficient financial resources, I will offer a sum of money to reward and help the young people with thoughts and talents, so that they can have a place to belong to and achieve success in their studies, and create great careers for the society and the country. I hope that the powerful people in the society will advocate this. It is truly immeasurable merit. Like the United States, there are many rich people who donate their estates to famous universities to cultivate promising young people. Is it possible that we Chinese cannot do this great plan for cultivating people for a hundred years?"

The Lament of Ancient Chinese Heroic Female Poets (III) 257

— Kang Tun

Separation in life, death, longing for spring, late years, unrequited love, abandonment, mismatched marriage, and chaos due to war. "Worship the new moon, worship the moon emerging from the hall; the dark spirit deeply imitates the cassia; the empty bow is not drawn... Worship the new moon, worship the moon with overwhelming emotion. The moon approaches as people grow old, and gazing at the moon prolongs life. The mother of the family to the east also worships the moon, and with each worship, her voice breaks with sorrow. In the past, she worshiped the moon to show off her beauty, but now she worships the single tear of vermilion. Looking back at the women worshiping the new moon, I recall my youth in the boudoir!"

In the song "Zhu Gong Qu" by Liu Cai Chun, a female poet from eastern Zhejiang appreciated by Yuan Wei Zhi, there is also a five-character poem lamenting old age:

"Yesterday was better than today, this year is older than last year. The Yellow River may become clear one day, but there is no chance for white hair to turn black!"

The Lament of Unrequited Love

A scholar dies for his confidant, and a woman adorns herself for her admirer. It is also the most unbearable thing in a woman's psychology to pity herself and not be able to gain the favor of her lover. Lady Hou, a palace maid of Emperor Yang of Sui, hanged herself out of resentment for not being able to be favored by the emperor. She had a brocade pouch tied to her arm, which contained a poem:

"Adorned with much self-pity, good dreams turn into sorrow. Not as good as the meaning of willow catkins, flying wherever spring arrives."

"Wanting to cry but unable to shed tears, grief turns into forced song, the flowers in the courtyard are blooming brilliantly, but there is no way to deal with spring!"

Wu Zetian, as an extraordinary female hero, had countless male favorites, and also had poems of unrequited love. Her "Ru Yi Qu" says:

"Seeing red as green, thoughts are chaotic, haggard and distraught for the sake of billions of subjects.

If you don't believe that I often shed tears lately, open the box and examine the pomegranate skirt." Emperor Ming of Tang initially favored Consort Mei, Jiang Cai Ping, but later favored Yang Tai Zhen, and moved Consort Mei to Shangyang Palace. When an envoy from a foreign country presented pearls, Emperor Ming bestowed a bushel of them to Consort Mei, who responded with a poem:

"Cassia leaves and eyebrows have not been painted for a long time, residual makeup mixed with tears wets the red silk, spending the whole day without combing, why bother consoling with pearls!"

The Lament of Abandonment

Mandarin ducks and phoenixes in harmony, growing old together, this is the happiest couple in the world. However, there are countless infatuated men and resentful women in the world. At first, there were oaths of love, but in the end, the mandarin ducks and phoenixes drifted apart. In a feudal society that valued men over women, the abandoned women could only swallow their tears and remain silent, with no law to appeal to. Under the cage of old ethics, they still had to maintain their reputation and self-restraint. From the following poems, one can imagine the sorrow of the generally abandoned women in ancient times.

"Mandarin ducks are on the beam, folding their left wings. This person is unkind, changing their virtue again and again!" (Poem Bai Hua, seven chapters. King You of Zhou obtained Bao Si and deposed Queen Shen, so the people of Zhou wrote this poem.)

"Newly torn Qi fine silk, as white and clean as frost and snow, cut into a fan of conjugal bliss, round like the bright moon. Entering and exiting your sleeves, swaying with a gentle breeze. Often fearing the arrival of autumn, cool winds take away the heat, discarded in the bamboo chest, affection and love severed halfway!"

(During the reign of Emperor Cheng of Han, Ban Jie Yu was slandered by Zhao Fei Yan's sisters. Jie Yu feared danger, so she served the Empress Dowager in Changxin Palace and wrote the poem of the silk fan.)

"Lonely white rabbit, running east and looking west. Clothes are not as good as new, people are not as good as old!" (Song of Complaint by Han Bao Yuan's Wife)

"Who says the divorced wife is gone? The divorced wife's feelings are even stronger. One should not spit in a well a thousand miles away, let alone what was previously served! Looking far is not painful, hesitating but unable to share." (Wei Liu Dong's wife, Wang Song, was divorced for being childless and wrote this poem.)

"Who does not love the beauty of spring flowers, but eventually they are hurt when they fall in autumn. The smoke from the chimney still lowers itself, and it is not expected to be humble and retreat! Cassia fragrance is in vain, losing love is in the moth eyebrows. Sitting and watching the beautiful season end, haggard and mocking myself in vain!" (Song of Complaint after Jin Shi Chong's maid Xiang Feng was abandoned.)

The Lament of Mismatched Marriage

In ancient times, marriages were based on the orders of parents and the words of matchmakers, not by the choice of the person involved; or even if they were self-chosen, they were still blind. Therefore, whether due to incompatible personalities or unmatched talents and appearance, there was the sorrow of a colorful phoenix following a crow, and precious jade falling into filth. The man-eating ethics of staying together until death shackled them so that they could not escape. A dumb person eating coptis chinensis, unable to express their suffering, such as Zhuang Jiang of Wei in the Three Hundred Poems; and Li Qing Zhao and Zhu Shu Zhen among the female poets of the Song Dynasty, can be said to be representatives of this.

The Burden of Multiple Births 258

Class Struggle (Part 2) 259

— Yin

Wen Feng, needless to say, was definitely a top-notch modern Shanghai lady. Since she was so careful in selecting maids for their beauty, how could she not pay attention to her own beauty? Because she was beautiful, her female classmates and friends were naturally very beautiful too; moreover, she was secretly dating a handsome lover!

Under the favor of her mistress, Xiang Lin naturally worked very hard. She inevitably gossiped a bit, but that could be ignored. However, she was originally a flirtatious person. Since entering the He family and spending every day with Wen Feng and her group of friends, her desire for extravagance and vanity grew stronger day by day. In addition, Xiang Lin treated her very politely, so everyone dared not treat her as a servant. She was truly extremely free. When she first came, she wore short clothes, but later she changed to long cheongsams, and even high heels. Needless to say, she permed her hair and wore makeup. Her looks were originally above Wen Feng's, and now that she had put so much effort into dressing up, she completely overshadowed Wen Feng. Outsiders who didn't know the details couldn't guess that they were mistress and servant.

"Look, Xiang Lin from the He family is even more beautiful than Wen Feng herself..."

"Isn't Xiang Lin's appearance a standard beauty? How can Wen Feng compare..."

Gradually, these kinds of words were whispered in everyone's mouths, and eventually they reached Wen Feng's ears. This naturally made her very unhappy. No matter how much she loved Xiang Lin, she couldn't tolerate people saying that she herself was not as beautiful as Xiang Lin. But she had chosen her herself, so how could she chase her away now? So she had to secretly use a passive means to deal with her. First, she restricted her from wearing makeup, saying that the old master didn't like it; second, she restricted her from wearing high heels, saying that the old lady disliked the sound of her walking. Xiang Lin naturally had to obey, so she changed to wearing a pair of embroidered satin shoes, and without makeup, she revealed her original exquisite face. Oh! This was even more beautiful! Wen Feng still thought it was too eye-catching, so she went a step further and restricted her from perming her hair. In this way, Xiang Lin simply didn't cut her hair and, after a few months, tied up her hair into a bun herself. Who knew that people thought she was even more beautiful. People up and down the He family were surprisingly exclaiming, "Xiang Lin is even more beautiful now, just like a young mistress."

A young mistress, of course, has the kind of beauty of a young mistress. Wen Feng carefully observed that Xiang Lin's beauty had indeed taken on a kind of beauty of a young mistress. At the same time, she also discovered that she had to change her embroidered satin shoes almost every five days, and she bought a lot of things, as if she had plenty of money; she often asked for leave on Saturdays and Sundays, and her words were not as soft as before. Wen Feng therefore became extremely suspicious. Later, she suddenly discovered that her own lover's attitude towards her was gradually becoming indifferent. If he called and Xiang Lin answered the phone, he would often talk for a few minutes. Wen Feng questioned him, but he denied it. But one day, she finally found her lover in a movie theater with Xiang Lin, sitting shoulder to shoulder and whispering, looking just like a newly married couple. Wen Feng was furious. When the movie ended, she deliberately waited at the exit; who knew that the two of them walked away hand in hand, as if they hadn't seen her at all.

Wen Feng returned home with a livid face. She threw all of Xiang Lin's things out of the door and wanted to wait for her to come back and beat her severely, but she waited until dawn and Xiang Lin didn't come back. From then on, she officially went to live with Wen Feng's lover and practice the love of cohabitation.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Reading the Newspaper 260

— I

Yesterday, after dinner, I had nothing to do, so I picked up a Shen Bao newspaper to read. In terms of foreign news, I saw that Li Bai had proposed peace terms, requesting the central government to give him a nominal position to go abroad, and that Chairman Jiang had telegraphed Li Bai again, urging him to leave Gui as soon as possible and take up his new position. I was very happy to read this. According to this situation, the Gui army's changes are likely to be resolved peacefully. If so, it is admirable that Li Bai has such a deep understanding of the overall situation.

Later, I also read that the Japanese were deeply infiltrating Ningxia and Gansu, organizing special agencies in various banners, and conducting activities in Alxa Banner, Pingliang, and other places. I also read that the Japanese Consulate in Tianjin was planning a program to expand the police power in North China. I also read that Japanese ruffians were setting up factories in Tianjin and privately manufacturing drugs. I also read that the Japanese army in the Japanese concession in Tianjin was practicing street fighting. I also read that the Japanese navy was preparing a new national defense plan to dominate the Pacific. I also read the current commentary on the issue of Japan arbitrarily establishing a consulate general in Chengdu. I unknowingly slammed the teacup in my hand onto the patio with a bang, shattering it into thirteen thousand nine hundred and ninety-nine pieces.

I didn't like reading such news. I turned around to look at world news. The first item was that the Afghan people were not giving up and continued to fiercely resist the Italian army. Forty thousand Afghan troops advanced towards Taixi. It was rare for the Afghan people to have such a hard-working spirit. The second item was that Britain and Germany expressed their approval of non-interference in Spanish internal affairs, but Germany required the same acceptance by the Soviet Union as a condition, while Italy had not yet replied and its attitude was unclear. The third item was the truth about the Italian plane, and the French investigation was completed, proving that it belonged to the regular Italian air force. The fourth item was that German warships had arrived at the Port of Ceuta, but according to the German Ministry of the Army, the purpose was to protect overseas Chinese. Looking at the situation of various countries competing with each other, Spain was unlikely to be the fuse for the Second World War, and I couldn't help but take seventeen or eighteen breaths of cold air.

Reading domestic news was so frustrating, and reading foreign news was so irritating. I thought I would look at the local news, which would definitely be more interesting. Let's read the price! First, Japanese sailors continued to investigate evidence of rural construction; second, the old Taoist Gao Lianliang of Zhunlian Society, the shameful father and son suing each other; third, bandits robbing Xiang Sheng's car; fourth, a socialite in Suzhou suing for abandonment and the judgment; fifth, two men and women throwing themselves into the river, and Liu Zhengxing being accused; eighth, two boys from Zhabei being abducted in Xiamen, and their families being invited to come and identify them; ninth, Xu Deyu's nephew, abducting and hiding his young daughter; tenth, a traveler in a Wuxi hotel taking poison. Ah! The situation in Shanghai society is so bad, either adultery or theft, either abduction or fraud, either drugs or murder. What kind of society is this?

Originally, I didn't read the newspaper much. Today, I happened to read the newspaper, and the impressions I discovered everywhere are like this. If I read the previous newspapers, I am afraid there will be many situations even worse than today's. The old accounts can be ignored. If I want to read the newspaper again in the future, I am afraid that the situation will continue to deteriorate. It is also unknown. The only thing that is barely satisfactory is that Li Bai proposed peace terms and requested the central government to give him a nominal position to go abroad. However, whether it can be implemented remains to be seen in the future. Therefore, I do not want to read the newspaper next time.

Days of Hardship 261

— Lin Na

We received a telegram from the provincial government saying that the Moro people had rebelled. For the sake of my job, I was sent by the newspaper to cover the story.

This place belongs to part of Moro Province. The uprising took place in a small town. This town has only a short street, densely packed with hundreds of low zinc houses. Chinese and Japanese merchants live in the houses. These merchants exist by exchanging very low-priced foreign goods for coconuts and grains from the inland.

A broken freight car loaded me up, swinging on the hillside like a pendulum. The driver was a local, a dark and short man around forty years old. He timidly told me:

"People who are used to living in big cities would never dream that such a thing would happen here..." He sighed lowly, his face a little pale. "They are not human, but beasts. Just think: they are all naked, with red cloth strips tied around their heads. In the middle of the night, they rushed into the town like bees. Then, the whole town was filled with shouts. People screamed and cried in confusion. In the darkness, nothing could be distinguished. It was all dark people, naked people jumping around. From time to time, only a few rays of knife light flashed..." He shook his head again. After thinking deeply for a while, he murmured again, "This is a miracle, sir, it hasn't been seen for more than thirty years..."

There is a church here, but it has already been surrounded by rioters with wood and burned down. The fire has not yet been extinguished. The open space is full of charcoal smells and rubble. Four or five police officers are directing a large number of workers. Starting excavation work, because several Spanish priests were buried alive in the rubble.

"This is a great misfortune!" I went to visit the police chief of the town branch, a tall middle-aged man. He first waved his hand, and then shouted in an excited tone, "But we have done our best to fulfill our responsibilities. Heaven is my witness. From the beginning to the end, I spent all my energy leading the only twelve police officers to fight against those one thousand rioters... And now, it's all over, like a flash of lightning..."

His face trembled slightly, and then he smiled solemnly.

"I hope you can tell me the reason for this uprising," I asked.

"This," he frowned deeply, thought for a while, and then continued, "This is very clear. Three Japanese shops, united to deceive a group of Moro people. First, the merchants shouted like this, when those natives brought large quantities of coconuts from the inland.

—We are very welcome, old friends! Can you allow me to pay a special price to keep your goods?

—Yes, we are very willing! The Moro people answered in cheerful tones.

—Then weigh them! Then the merchants took out the scale that could turn one hundred and fifty pounds of goods into one hundred and five pounds. I'm sorry, sir, I have to explain that the Chinese and Japanese merchants here live on this. Without this, they can't survive, they really can't survive. Finally, these merchants gave him a few fun items and said gently:

—Good friends, the coconuts have been weighed. In two days, just two more days, you can come here to get what you want...

The Moro people were very satisfied with this answer, gently took those fun items with their hands, stroked them for a while, and walked away with them in their arms. But after a few days, they went down the mountain to get what they wanted, but found that the zinc houses were empty, and the merchants had moved away, so they returned to the mountain with disappointed faces. After a few days like this, the incident happened..."

At this time, someone hurried in, so I said goodbye to leave. He followed me happily behind and sent me away.

"I'm sorry, I can't entertain you properly. If Manila wants to publish this news, please add a few words for me: Marlor, the police chief of Zhi Luo Town, did his duty and bravely quelled the three thousand rioters with twelve police officers in the dark night..."

I said that I would be happy to serve him. We shook hands and parted ways.

On the street, I walked slowly. Many of the low, neat zinc houses had been burned down. Only a few dozen remained. The doors were tightly closed. In one open grocery store, a dozen Chinese people were huddled together, arguing about something. They all had weapons in their hands: such as broadswords, short wooden sticks, pistols... It is said that in order to defend against these rioters from coming to disturb them again, they had armed themselves, ready to help the brave police chief pacify the rebellion when necessary.

But an old Chinese man told me with a worried tone: "Our efforts may be in vain. These natives are very brave, and when they come in, it's like a tide. Just the cowhide drum, the shouts! It's enough to scare us." After a pause, he said again: "In order to resist, we have had twelve people killed, including five whose heads are missing..." He was very worried, sinking into unease and depression, his eyes shooting out light of terror and despair.

Next to a small house not far away, there was a sorrowful woman's wail, slowly seeping through. The old man pointed with his finger and shook his head in despair, saying: "This is one of those who were killed, young, his wife had only just come from Tangshan, but she encountered this disaster. It's been three days, and the head hasn't been found yet..." I also shook my head in sympathy. He was silent for a while before murmuring in a low voice:

"This is a year of hardship..." I looked up at him, and his eye sockets were already overflowing with tears.

Page 22

Perfume Thieves (Continued) 262

— Qi Ying

When they heard us say that we saw them in the valley ahead, they hurried forward.

Our hearts were beating wildly. I grabbed the last person and asked, "What are you asking those two people to do?"

"Those two people are perfume thieves. They have a kind of incense that makes you faint when you smell it. They have committed two cases in Xingzi County and even killed someone!"

We few young partners were all stunned. As if we saw those two pairs of glowing, terrible eyes, we felt that there was an atmosphere of terror in the mountains and fields. Our bodies were soaked in sweat again, but it was a cold sweat. (Note: Jiangxi people commonly refer to strangers)

Trunk 263

— Leon

"The 28th... Today is the 19th... Tomorrow is the 20th, the day after tomorrow the 21st, the day after that the 22nd, 23rd, 24th... only nine days from beginning to end!" Little Gendi calculated in her heart almost every day. She always felt dissatisfied, having toiled through wind, frost, rain, and snow since she was small. At eleven years old, the day of her marriage was only nine days away. But her mother still urged her to work every day, still wore that same ramie cloth shirt, still piled her hair on her head like a bird's nest, nothing had changed.

Her mother and father seemed to have forgotten about Little Gendi's wedding, each busy with their own work every day. How resentful she felt.

In front of the sock knitting machine, Little Gendi kept thinking:

What are Mom and Dad really thinking? If they don't want to marry their daughter off, why did they accept the betrothal gifts so early? Now they've spent the other family's money and act as if nothing happened. It's simply too muddled. Even if the dowry isn't anything grand, there should at least be a few small pieces of furniture, some seasonal clothes... and two trunks. When the day comes, do they expect me to go empty-handed to their house?" Heavy thoughts weighed her down, and her work suffered.

She returned home with a tired body and an unhappy mood. The matchmaker, Wang, was sitting on her mother's bed, discussing something with her. She didn't dare to brazenly go closer, or her father would scold her for being "shameless." While stoking the stove and stewing porridge, she eavesdropped on her mother and Wang's conversation. They were discussing the matter of trunks. How stingy her mother was, completely refusing the three trunks that Wang had requested. She even said things like, "If they take my daughter away so early, who will subsidize our old couple's expenses every month? We'll have to work our old bones to the bone. I can't afford to buy this and that." That night, the matchmaker, Wang, left unhappily.

"Mom, could it be that not even one... one... trunk... will be taken over there? They spent money too... How will I face them in the future..." Little Gendi couldn't bear it any longer and said to her mother.

These words, however, pricked her father's anger like needles: "Shameless, shameless! You still mention money? Wasn't that money used up by you two little devils when you caught the plague? One died, and you, this living treasure, were left, and now you're going to be splashed away like water. I raised you, hoping to rely on you for a few days, but damn it, it's all in vain. You want to put on a show, but you chose the wrong life. Don't you know your parents are poor!"

After a scolding, Little Gendi sat by the stove, sobbing.

Her mother, after all, loved her daughter. (And her father didn't not love his daughter; it was just that their poor life was too ruthless.) Little Gendi heard her mother's loving voice: "Forgive your poor mom and dad. Who isn't strained by money? Fortunately, Gendi, a person has their fate determined. Your destiny is set. In the future, not to mention trunks, even a large wardrobe will be easy to come by. Your fate is set to be bitter. Even if you have gold, silver, pearls, and treasures now, they will all be used up and gone. Once you go over there, as long as your husband is well-behaved and you yourself are frugal and hardworking, trunks will be easy to get..."

Little Gendi slightly suppressed her sadness, looking at her mother with tearful eyes.

"But, you must understand that your dad isn't such a heartless person. He knows you've been working since you were small, helping the family survive. He just doesn't have money, and besides, when you go to their house, the family's expenses will be even more... His temper is getting worse and worse..." Four streams of tears fell together...

Window 264

— Menghua

Across from my room is a window, a small window, separated by a small alley.

The distance between our two windows is only about half a zhang. At night, when the lights in the surrounding houses are all extinguished, the tangerine-yellow light from the window across the way seems particularly warm. I love that window; it's like a riddle, giving me many insights: How fleeting life is!

When I first moved in, I started to notice that window. It was so intimate! From that small window opening, I saw the face of a kind mother, holding a baby less than a year old in her arms. The low lullaby put her son to sleep and also mesmerized me. A traveler who had lost his mother's caresses received motherly love from here.

However, soon after, at night, that window was buried in the boundless darkness, with no shadow and no sound, as desolate as an ancient tomb. The unbearable loneliness struck me. So, I often closed my own window and added a layer of white cloth. Although the room was stuffy, I felt at ease. I feared that window, I feared that boundless darkness.

Not long after, a foreign little girl's pale face appeared in the window across the way. She often leaned against the window, gazing at me with her blue eyes. Her father was a drunkard all day long, his body as dirty as a loach just pulled out of the mud, his disheveled beard, his hoarse voice, made me feel that he was a down-and-out person. At midnight, that window was still bright and open, with the sounds of sobs and curses flowing over from time to time.

A month later, this family hurriedly moved away again. I saw the man carrying a broken box in his hand, the woman carrying a bundle of odds and ends on her back. And then that little girl's face became blurred, as if I had seen it only in a dream.

Perhaps someone else will move in soon! Perhaps my tearful eyes will see some strange aspects of the world again! I must thank this window; it allows me to see the various faces of human life. Life, how bizarre and ever-changing! As if chasing after something. People come and go in a hurry. Where are they ultimately going? These untiring travelers of life!

Prison Song

The shackles in prison extinguish people's happiness; the life in prison collects people's sins into a net. Surely there are some fierce demons still arbitrarily killing and setting fires. Pitiful are some innocent Buddhas, suffering and being tormented in prison. Some are oppressed, some are instigated, living locked in this prison. Whose voice will speak of your dull pain? In bitterness, you hold grievances; whose voice will explain for you? To live is to betray the joy of life, forever unable to wash away wrongs and mistakes. To die! You leave behind wives, children, and parents, full of sorrow, with no one to entrust your words to. Shameful human demons, pitiful human Buddhas, one day will destroy the world.
